Med."], "published-print": {"date-parts": [[2008, 1]]}, "abstract": "<jats:title>Abstract</jats:title><jats:p>Polycystic ovarian syndrome (PCOS) is universally recognised as the commonest endocrinopathy of women. The definition and the aetiological hypotheses of PCOS are continuously evolving to accommodate expanding knowledge on the syndrome, which is now known to be more complex than purely a reproductive disorder. Increased androgen synthesis, disrupted folliculogenesis and insulin resistance lie at the pathophysiological core of PCOS. An intriguing concept involves the perpetuation of a vicious circle with endocrine/reproductive and metabolic components. An unfavourable metabolic environment may unmask genetic traits of ovarian dysfunction, and the unfolding endocrine derangement could further aggravate the metabolic disarray. This article reviews the molecular mechanisms known to underlie the ovarian and metabolic abnormalities characterising PCOS. The putative interdependence between reproductive and metabolic aspects of PCOS, and therapeutic implications for the management of PCOS, are also discussed.</jats:p>", "DOI": The association between insulin resistance and PCOS has led to the discovery that insulin is an important reproductive hormone and that insulin signaling in the CNS is critical for ovulation. The concept of secondary PCOS implies that there is a primary well-defined cause leading to the PCOS phenotype with underlying androgen overproduction, regardless of the origin. In these cases, we presume the term of \u2018secondary PCOS\u2019 could be used. In all these conditions, the potential complete recovery of the hyperandrogenemic state as well as the remission of the PCOS phenotype should follow the removal of the cause. If accepted, these concepts could help clinicians to perform in-depth investigations of the potential factors or disorders responsible for the development of these specific forms of secondary PCOS. Sixteen obese women with PCOS on a weight-maintaining diet were studied before and after 6 months of therapy with the insulin-sensitizing antidiabetic agent metformin at a dose of 1700 mg per day. Compared with baseline values, glucose utilization was markedly enhanced at 6 months using the two-step euglycaemic-hyperinsulinaemic clamp to measure changes in insulin sensitivity (2.56 +/- 0.32 vs 4.68 +/- 0.49 mg/kg per min, P = 0.0001, when 40 mU insulin/m2 per min was infused, and 6.48 +/- 0.58 vs 9.84 +/- 0.72 mg/kg per min, P = 0.0002, when 400 mU insulin insulin/m2 per min was infused). The improvement in insulin action was accompanied by significant increases in the levels of sex hormone-binding globulin (24.5 +/- 7.2 vs 39.8 +/- 16.2 nmol/l, P = 0.003) and decreases in free testosterone (12.8 +/- 5.8 vs 9.0 +/- 3.0 pmol/l, P = 0.03) and androstenedione (12.9 +/- 5.6 vs 7.3 +/- 1.7 nmol/l, P = 0.003). No significant changes were recorded in body weight. Seven subjects resumed normal menstruation and two cases of spontaneous pregnancy occurred during treatment. Metformin was well tolerated except for one case of flatulence. These results confirm that metformin treatment can lead to improvements in insulin resistance and ovarian hyperandrogenism.</jats:p>", "DOI": "10.1530/eje.0.1380269", "type": "journal-article", "created": {"date-parts": [[2005, 1, 24]], "date-time": "2005-01-24T21:34:41Z", "timestamp": 1106602481000}, "page": "269-274", "update-policy": "http://dx.doi.org/10.1530/crossmarkpolicy-1", "source": "Crossref", "is-referenced-by-count": 180, "title": ["Therapeutic effects of metformin on insulin resistance and hyperandrogenism in polycystic ovary syndrome"], "prefix": "10.1530", "author": [{"given": "E", "family": "Diamanti-Kandarakis", "sequence": "first", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "C", "family": "Kouli", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "T", "family": "Tsianateli", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "A", "family": "Bergiele", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}], "member": "416", "container-title": ["European Journal of Endocrinology"], "link": [{"URL": "https://eje.bioscientifica.com/view/journals/eje/138/3/269.xml", "content-type": "text/html", "content-version": "vor", "intended-application": "text-mining"}], "deposited": {"date-parts": [[2019, 2, 19]], "date-time": "2019-02-19T12:33:50Z", "timestamp": 1550579630000}, "score": 28.89743, "issued": {"date-parts": [[1998, 3, 1]]}, "references-count": 0, "URL": "http://dx.doi.org/10.1530/eje.0.1380269", "ISSN": ["0804-4643", "1479-683X"], "issn-type": [{"value": "0804-4643", "type": "print"}, {"value": "1479-683X", "type": "electronic"}]}], "items-per-page": 20, "query": {"start-index": 0, "search-terms": null}}}
